    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826047602?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826047602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10374551448595322087"><i>The Thing About Jellyfish</i> is a young adult book centered on grief at a young age. Suzy, “Zu”, loses her best friend and in dealing with this tragic, unexpected loss, decides to minimize her speaking with the outside world. <br/><br/>It’s definitely a YA story but a touching one, that reminds readers of the traditionally tough age and mindset of middle-schoolers, and that everyone deals with grief in different ways. I also enjoyed the elements of Zu’s curiosity and interest in learning - Science was never </span>
  <span id="freeText10374551448595322087" style="display:none"><i>The Thing About Jellyfish</i> is a young adult book centered on grief at a young age. Suzy, “Zu”, loses her best friend and in dealing with this tragic, unexpected loss, decides to minimize her speaking with the outside world. <br /><br />It’s definitely a YA story but a touching one, that reminds readers of the traditionally tough age and mindset of middle-schoolers, and that everyone deals with grief in different ways. I also enjoyed the elements of Zu’s curiosity and interest in learning - Science was never a favorite subject of mine, but the curious concepts are universal and can be applied to any area of interest. <br /><br />While <i>The Thing About Jellyfish</i> wasn’t one of my all-time favorites, I appreciated this story, which was also a quick read.</span>

<div id="review_1350642219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1350642219" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1350642219?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=science">science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=disaster">disaster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=dysfunctional-family">dysfunctional-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=school">school</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1350642219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16429111755567833779">This frankly very strange yet wonderful middle-grade novel focuses on several themes, including grief, science and social isolation. How much is too much when it comes to mourning? When does loss become an obsession? How far should kids be pushed to say goodbye and let go of the past? These questioned are all addressed whilst Suzy tries her best to cling onto something she can understand. With the help of a caring teacher, she finds solace in science and starts learning how to move on. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7223626712851998570">This book should be sold with a pack of kleenex. At least when it's being purchased by an adult. Kids will do just fine I suspect.<br/><br/>It is a warm and wonderful blend of healing from loss, dealing with being in middle school and not fitting in, learning that you have the power to hurt someone and you won't always have the chance to make it up to them. It's about the beauty of science, the ecology of our planet. It's about the nature of bravery and heroism and family and love. So, I guess it's about </span>
  <span id="freeText7223626712851998570" style="display:none">This book should be sold with a pack of kleenex. At least when it's being purchased by an adult. Kids will do just fine I suspect.<br /><br />It is a warm and wonderful blend of healing from loss, dealing with being in middle school and not fitting in, learning that you have the power to hurt someone and you won't always have the chance to make it up to them. It's about the beauty of science, the ecology of our planet. It's about the nature of bravery and heroism and family and love. So, I guess it's about pretty much everything which may seem impossible in a 300 page novel for middle grade readers, but it seems to me that is the job of all the best books regardless of the targeted age of their audiences.<br /><br />This title has been getting a lot of buzz (Indies Introduce, BEA Middle Grade Buzz selection) and in my opinion, it deserves it. Plus, if you read it you'll pick up some very interesting facts about jellyfish that I'm pretty sure you don't already know -- useful at any age.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7066303305458449886">This is a lovely YA book about a child's first encounter with the mourning process. Bereavement is never easy, but for children it seems to be particularly confusing. Benjamin tells us the story of a young teenage girl who loses her best friend and the difficulties she encounters coming to terms with this loss.<br/><br/>It may be that I have not been a teenager for a while, but some of the passages seemed unnecessarily long to me. But when I asked my students about the pacing of this book they all liked i</span>
  <span id="freeText7066303305458449886" style="display:none">This is a lovely YA book about a child's first encounter with the mourning process. Bereavement is never easy, but for children it seems to be particularly confusing. Benjamin tells us the story of a young teenage girl who loses her best friend and the difficulties she encounters coming to terms with this loss.<br /><br />It may be that I have not been a teenager for a while, but some of the passages seemed unnecessarily long to me. But when I asked my students about the pacing of this book they all liked it enormously! So it definitely works for the target audience! Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_3060709970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3060709970" />
    <a title="andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100778714-andrea"><img alt="andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604665131p2/100778714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3060709970?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="andrea" href="/user/show/100778714-andrea">andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who enjoyed Counting By 7s; kids who were bullied in middle school for being studious</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=books-that-i-own">books-that-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=a-group-of-characters-pissed-me-off">a-group-of-characters-pissed-me-off</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=loved-the-characters">loved-the-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=made-me-anxious-for-the-story">made-me-anxious-for-the-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=bechdel-test">bechdel-test</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=middle-grade-that-i-read-now">middle-grade-that-i-read-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/100778714-andrea?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3060709970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6896388696436530040">The whole theme of this book is that people deal with loss in different ways. Did I expect this middle-grade book to handle loss the way a YA book would? No. So was I very pleasantly surprised? Yes.<br/>My mom actually bought this book for me when I was in fifth grade because it was "on-sale", so I've just had it lying inside my bookshelf for years. It came to my attention to read it about a year ago but I only ever managed to read it now. I honestly didn't expect it to be that great, because my best</span>
  <span id="freeText6896388696436530040" style="display:none">The whole theme of this book is that people deal with loss in different ways. Did I expect this middle-grade book to handle loss the way a YA book would? No. So was I very pleasantly surprised? Yes.<br />My mom actually bought this book for me when I was in fifth grade because it was "on-sale", so I've just had it lying inside my bookshelf for years. It came to my attention to read it about a year ago but I only ever managed to read it now. I honestly didn't expect it to be that great, because my best friend read it in fifth grade and I literally never heard her talk about it, so I assumed it was kind of sucky.<br />It reminded me of the book "Counting By 7s" by Holly Goldberg Sloan. Both books handled with loss and genius outcast girls. Both books randomly spit out science facts at every corner but made it work for the story.<br />This book is about a girl named Suzy Swanson who, although it isn't explicitly stated in the book, is a genius. You can pretty much infer that from the start. Now, whether the not that was the explanation for why she severely lacked social skills and thought factually rather than logically and emotionally, I don't know. The whole time reading I got the vibe that maybe she had a social disability or something of the sort. Despite that, her ex-best friend had just died, and after jumping to a few conclusions, Suzy is convinced that a jellyfish has killed her. One of the reasons this book is so beautiful is because of Suzy's naivete. She doesn't realize that her facts and her science are making people laugh at her. She has also resorted to not talking to anybody, including her parents, not because she is traumatized, well, partially that, but simply because she doesn't want to. I think Suzy is such a good main character because my sixth-grade self could strongly relate to her throughout this book. She is charming and sweet but is so misunderstood and gets made fun of for just being herself, which hurts. She is very thorough (and when I say VERY thorough) and loves to research and figure things out scientifically. She is a perfectionist and frowns at failure. She has been deeply affected by her friend's crush on a boy and doesn't want things to change. This was all me in seventh grade. She did seem to appear younger though, but I think that just might be the point of the character. <br />One issue I did have with this book was the way the dialogue was written. There was seemingly no variation, besides Suzy's internal dialogue, in the way everyone spoke. Sure, they could be mean, they could be kind, they could be just giving a report, but it all felt like the same person was talking each time. The dialogue was also handled in a sort of "after school special" kind of way. Don't get me wrong, "Sesame Street" is great, but not if a twelve-year-old boy is talking to a girl his age in that manner, the same way her parent or her teacher or her older brother would talk to her.<br />Overall, I really did enjoy this book. Suzy's drive to prove what happened to her best friend and her whole emotional journey to discover why that really matters was so well done. I would recommend this to anyone between 10 years old to 15 years old, as I think those are the ones who would receive optimal enjoyment from this book. Also, I think the prologue was just beautiful. It was jaw-dropping and it really told me that I would enjoy the book. As a whole, I was pleasantly surprised.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6896388696436530040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1494743405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494743405" />
    <a title="Aoife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife"><img alt="Aoife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514771423p2/16768476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1494743405?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife">Aoife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316380836" href="/book/show/25851271-the-thing-about-jellyfish">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=2016-favourites">2016-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=best-2016">best-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=better-than-expected">better-than-expected</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494743405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13161001944571180983">I received a free digital copy from the author/publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest feedback.<br/><br/>Suzy is 13 years old and dealing with the death of her best friend who drowned during the summer. When Suzy discovers the vast world of the jellyfish, she decides that a jellyfish sting must be why Franny died and sets out to prove it to the world.<br/><br/>I wasn't expecting to love this book as much as I did but I absolutely adored it. It was much faster-paced than I expected too. I think because I </span>
  <span id="freeText13161001944571180983" style="display:none">I received a free digital copy from the author/publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest feedback.<br /><br />Suzy is 13 years old and dealing with the death of her best friend who drowned during the summer. When Suzy discovers the vast world of the jellyfish, she decides that a jellyfish sting must be why Franny died and sets out to prove it to the world.<br /><br />I wasn't expecting to love this book as much as I did but I absolutely adored it. It was much faster-paced than I expected too. I think because I knew there were a lot of jellyfish facts in it, I thought i would get a bit bogged down in them and it would slow down my reading but nope. I finished this book in one sitting.<br /><br />Ultimately this is a book about a girl who has just started her teenage years and discovering that the world is a much vaster and confusing place than she originally thought. And with Franny's death, Suzy has to confront the fact that dying is something that happens to young people, and that sometimes things like that just happen for no reason at all.<br /><br />I really found myself identifying with Suzy. Particularly her issues with friends and everyone growing up that bit faster than her. Her confusion over the sudden gap between her and Franny and why she was suddenly left behind while the girls did their make-up and flirted with the boys. I think a lot of people could feel for Suzy in this one, as she's not the only person who's ever felt left behind.<br /><br />I loved Suzy's relationships as well. Her family were all amazing. Yes, they did bring her to a therapist to talk about the not talking situation but they never pushed her, or grew frustrated with her. They were there waiting, ready for when she was ready to accept everything and be there for her when she did. Her brother and his boyfriend, yes. I love how there was no big deal about Aaron being gay. There was no in depth story about him coming out or any controversy in the family because of it. Her parents were divorced but still on talking terms, and seemed to still be on pretty good terms considering they were separated. I also loved Mrs Thurton and her quiet observations and suggestions. It's always great to see a good teacher/mentor-student relationship and a teacher really offering that safe haven for a student who just needs that time and space. Ans Justin was just lovely. I really loved his explanations of ADHD and how his medication helped.<br /><br />This book was such a pleasant surprise and I would really urge everyone to read it, just to see if it will surprise you too. And who knew there were so many interesting facts about jellyfish!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13161001944571180983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1527359456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527359456" />
    <a title="Dov Zeller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/440651-dov-zeller"><img alt="Dov Zeller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478090196p2/440651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527359456?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dov Zeller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dov Zeller" href="/user/show/440651-dov-zeller">Dov Zeller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440651-dov-zeller?shelf=fiction-21st-cen">fiction-21st-cen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440651-dov-zeller?shelf=existential-pain-and-angst">existential-pain-and-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440651-dov-zeller?shelf=middle-grade-ya">middle-grade-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440651-dov-zeller?shelf=ecosystems">ecosystems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440651-dov-zeller?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440651-dov-zeller?shelf=sciency-naturish">sciency-naturish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527359456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11715933103577640522">"A jellyfish, if you watch it long enough, begins to look like a heart beating." <br/><br/>So begins Ali Benjamin's first novel written from the perspective of a kid whose love of the natural and scientific world works as both a connective and disconnecting force in her life. <br/><br/>The story moves back and forth in time between 1) Suzy's present predicament, as she struggles to cope with the loss of her once best friend Franny, and her guilt over their last few interactions, and tries to find her voice after lo</span>
  <span id="freeText11715933103577640522" style="display:none">"A jellyfish, if you watch it long enough, begins to look like a heart beating." <br /><br />So begins Ali Benjamin's first novel written from the perspective of a kid whose love of the natural and scientific world works as both a connective and disconnecting force in her life. <br /><br />The story moves back and forth in time between 1) Suzy's present predicament, as she struggles to cope with the loss of her once best friend Franny, and her guilt over their last few interactions, and tries to find her voice after losing her best friend twice, first for being something of a social outsider and not saying any of the "right" things, and then, with more finality, because Franny has died 2) the history of that friendship (in most alternating chapters), which ended not so well and not too long before Franny drowns during summer vacation. <br /><br />Somehow as she goes through the process of trying to make sense of Franny's death, Suzy becomes obsessed with swimmers and jellyfish and decides that Franny was too strong of a swimmer to just drown. She decides Franny's death was caused by the sting of the Irukandji Jellyfish, one of the msot deadly in the world. Otherwise it just seems too random, implausible and scary (that a person she knew and loved, and a really good swimmer, too, could just drown while hanging out on the Maryland coastline.)<br /><br />I think my favorite thing about this novel was the fact that the protagonist is into sciency stuff and a bit of social misfit. I enjoyed reading about jellyfish (though now I'm afraid of the tiny Irukandji that is so small it's barely visible and yet the sting can be deadly) and Suzy's relationship with her family is very sweet. I was horrified by Franny's middle-school nightmarish treatment of Suzy and baffled by Suzy's limited and yet perfect, eloquent self-awareness. Maybe the first-person narration didn't fully work for me. The structure was okay, but all in all, the book felt pretty similar to other YA stuff I've read. I don't know. It's good. A good book. Not amazing, and sometimes downright strange or bizarrely sinister (the whole frozen pee situation) but for the most part, an enjoyable read that would like to make us believe that if we are in middle school and feel alone, we shouldn't despair. Study intesting facts about non-human animals and we will eventually find our people!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11715933103577640522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NrT73WZCTw+dFCMjIzOuRvHX+9+jAr25/Ju+z7bRBoV0BgmtjPlKD2i7BAsVwFPiaj0aJW1WTq7iJvoJ3oXhGw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
